                <div class="ptW7te" jsname="yjbGtf" aria-labelledby="i23" role="region">
                    <div style="word-wrap:break-word;line-break:after-white-space">I just saw that you used v2.0.3. So that’s OK.
                        <div><br></div>
                        <div>However, something concerns me is that your alignment is very short:</div>
                        <div><br></div>
                        <div>
                            <div style="margin:0px;font-stretch:normal;font-size:13px;line-height:normal;font-family:Menlo;color:rgb(242,242,242);background-color:rgb(0,0,0)"><span style="font-variant-ligatures:no-common-ligatures">Alignment has 4350 sequences with 225 columns, 225 distinct patterns</span></div>
                            <div style="margin:0px;font-stretch:normal;font-size:13px;line-height:normal;font-family:Menlo;color:rgb(242,242,242);background-color:rgb(0,0,0)"><span style="font-variant-ligatures:no-common-ligatures">224 parsimony-informative, 1 singleton sites, 0 constant sites</span></div>
                            <div><br></div>
                            <div>In that case, you shouldn’t use any complex models. I’d be very cautious even if you use a simple model — there is very little phylogenetic information in this alignment. So either add [many] more genes or reduce the number
                                of sequences, before phylogenetic inference.</div>
                            <div><br></div>
                            <div>Sorry about that,</div>
                            <div>Minh</div>
                        </div>

                <div class="ptW7te" jsname="yjbGtf" aria-labelledby="i35" role="region">
                    <div dir="ltr">
                        <div dir="ltr">Hi Alexey,
                            <div><br></div>
                        </div>
                        <div class="gmail_quote"></div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="DTXlsb">
                        <div dir="ltr">
                            <div class="gmail_quote">
                                <blockquote class="gmail_quote" style="margin:0px 0px 0px 0.8ex;border-left:1px solid rgb(204,204,204);padding-left:1ex">
                                    <div dir="ltr">
                                        <div>You mentioned that the number of sites in the alignment might be not sufficient to reliebly estimate model parameters. My alignment contains 4350 sequences. How I can estimate the reliability of obtained results?</div>
                                    </div>
                                </blockquote>
                                <div><br></div>
                            </div>
                        </div>
                    </div>
                    <div dir="ltr">
                        <div class="gmail_quote">
                            <div>You could simulate data that resemble the data you have (i.e. under the PMSF-type models, and alignments of the same length, number of rows, site rates, and information content that you have), and then test how well you can
                                recover trees when using PMSF models (as you have for your empirical data) when compared to other, simpler models. This is a standard procedure called a parametric bootstrap (just to help you find things via google!).</div>
                        </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="DTXlsb">
                        <div dir="ltr">
                            <div class="gmail_quote">
                                <div> </div>
                                <blockquote class="gmail_quote" style="margin:0px 0px 0px 0.8ex;border-left:1px solid rgb(204,204,204);padding-left:1ex">
                                    <div dir="ltr">
                                        <div>The log file contains the warning:</div>
                                        <div>&#39;WARNING: The mixture model might be overfitting because some mixture weights are estimated close to zero&#39;. Totally 6 out of 20 weights are zero. Is it really a problem? </div>
                                    </div>
                                </blockquote>
                                <div><br></div>
                            </div>
                        </div>
                    </div>
                    <div dir="ltr">
                        <div class="gmail_quote">
                            <div>Yes.</div>
                        </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="DTXlsb">
                        <div dir="ltr">
                            <div class="gmail_quote">
                                <div> </div>
                                <blockquote class="gmail_quote" style="margin:0px 0px 0px 0.8ex;border-left:1px solid rgb(204,204,204);padding-left:1ex">
                                    <div dir="ltr">
                                        <div>Can I deal with it by reducing the number of classes in the model?</div>
                                    </div>
                                </blockquote>
                                <div><br></div>
                            </div>
                        </div>
                    </div>
                    <div dir="ltr">
                        <div class="gmail_quote">
                            <div>Potentially. But as Minh said, 225 informative sites is very very little information. At the very least I would recommend comparing a large range of models (focussing particularly on the most simple models) using standard approaches
                                like the AICc, BIC, etc. This will give you a good feeling for whether you can realistically justify parameter-rich models. </div>
                            <div> </div>
                            <div>Rob</div>
                            <div><br></div>

                <div class="ptW7te" jsname="yjbGtf" aria-labelledby="i41" role="region">Dear Alexey,
                    <br>
                    <br>Two additional comments in addition to those of Minh and Rob:
                    <br>
                    <div class="DTXlsb">
                        <br>&gt; On 28 Jun 2020, at 20:43, Alexey Neverov &lt;<a href data-email-masked rel="nofollow">neva...@gmail.com</a>&gt; wrote:
                        <br>&gt;
                        <br>&gt; The problem is somewhare in the &#39;-nt AUTO&#39; option. I sucsessfully processed this dataset when used fixed number of cores by specifying the &#39;-nt 16&#39; option. In the attachment the results of analysis.
                        <br>
                        <br></div>With only 225 sites in the alignment, parallelisation will not efficiently, meaning time savingly, work either.
                    <br>
                    <br>Typically, batches of sites are distributed to different processors. This causes some extra time to be required, e.g., for distributing the data and collecting the results. Hence, the batches have to be sufficiently large, to actually
                    save more time than is caused by this overhead.
                    <br>
                    <br>We have seen people enforcing high numbers of threads (cores) and then ended up with longer running times than when using only 1 core :(
                    <br>
                    <div class="DTXlsb">
                        <br>&gt; You mentioned that the number of sites in the alignment might be not sufficient to reliebly estimate model parameters. My alignment contains 4350 sequences. How I can estimate the reliability of obtained results?
                        <br>&gt; The log file contains the warning:
                        <br>
                        <br></div>Just one comment to think about. Assume all your sites would be informative to resolve parts of the tree. Furthermore, assume that each site can resolve one split (=branch) in the tree (something you typically cannot
                    achieve with real data). Then, your dataset would be able to only able to resolve 225 out of the 4347 branches in your final tree. All other branches would be more or less randomly resolved and might differ from run to run, because
                    there is no information in the data.
                    <br>
                    <br>The only way to resolve a higher percentage of branches reliably is either to add more sequence data to each taxon, e.g. more genes, or to reduce the number of sequences (the first thing here is typically to remove identical sequences
                    - this is also done already by IQ-TREE automatically and then re-added at the end, because here it is clear in what region of the tree they would end up, however, there is no way to determine their branching order in the tree.
                    <br>
                    <br>And as stressed by the others - with so short sequences you should not used complex models. You do not have enough information in the data for this.
                    <br>
                    <br>Best regards,
                    <br>Heiko
                    <br>

                                [1, [null, "With only 225 sites in the alignment, parallelisation will not efficiently, meaning time savingly, work either.\r\u003cbr\u003e\r\u003cbr\u003eTypically, batches of sites are distributed to different processors. This causes some extra time to be required, e.g., for distributing the data and collecting the results. Hence, the batches have to be sufficiently large, to actually save more time than is caused by this overhead.\r\u003cbr\u003e\r\u003cbr\u003eWe have seen people enforcing high numbers of threads (cores) and then ended up with longer running times than when using only 1 core :(\r\u003cbr\u003e"]],

                                [1, [null, "Just one comment to think about. Assume all your sites would be informative to resolve parts of the tree. Furthermore, assume that each site can resolve one split (\u003dbranch) in the tree (something you typically cannot achieve with real data). Then, your dataset would be able to only able to resolve 225 out of the 4347 branches in your final tree. All other branches would be more or less randomly resolved and might differ from run to run, because there is no information in the data.\r\u003cbr\u003e\r\u003cbr\u003eThe only way to resolve a higher percentage of branches reliably is either to add more sequence data to each taxon, e.g. more genes, or to reduce the number of sequences (the first thing here is typically to remove identical sequences - this is also done already by IQ-TREE automatically and then re-added at the end, because here it is clear in what region of the tree they would end up, however, there is no way to determine their branching order in the tree.\r\u003cbr\u003e\r\u003cbr\u003eAnd as stressed by the others - with so short sequences you should not used complex models. You do not have enough information in the data for this.\r\u003cbr\u003e\r\u003cbr\u003eBest regards,\r\u003cbr\u003eHeiko\r\u003cbr\u003e"]],
